Free Talk

Let's Give It a Try 183

— Mu Mutian

Dr. Hu Shih said in his "Essays on Experimentation" that "success has always come from experimentation." Although Dr. Hu Shih has now lost his position as a mentor to young people, the saying "success has always come from experimentation" is always worth savoring.

The spirit of "experimentation" is the spirit of the "May Fourth" Movement. The youth of China today must always have the spirit of "experimentation."

During the "May Fourth" era, progressive intellectuals opposed feudal classical Chinese and advocated vernacular Chinese. So they tried to create vernacular literature and brought out their own vernacular works. This practice of producing vernacular works was a good weapon for overthrowing classical Chinese. However, as the "May Fourth" tide subsided, the tendency of vernacular Chinese to become classical Chinese became increasingly developed.

The tendency of vernacular Chinese to become classical Chinese is a revival of the spirit of the late Ming Dynasty. This spirit has directly created the current "Yuan Zhonglangism" literature. This "Yuan Zhonglangism" is, of course, a literati literature. It is a disguised classical Chinese literature. It is probably in response to this "Zhonglangism" trend, and its brothers' trends, that the mass language literature movement was produced.

I have never expressed an opinion on mass language literature. But in the future society, there will definitely be the emergence of mass language literature, which is beyond doubt. However, in the current environment, there are quite a few difficulties in establishing mass language.

For the establishment of mass language literature, the environmental issue is a prerequisite. And the mass language of the future may be a kind of "scientific national language." Mass language should be comprehensive, not separate. And in China, it is necessary to produce a unified mass language. Naturally, there are exceptions for the Miao and Man peoples.

The proposal of the mass language issue is meaningful. However, up to now, the theory is still very conceptual and very vague. In order to help with this, I think everyone should work hard to practice the production of mass language literature. Naturally, there will be shortcomings and difficulties in the practice of production. However, the practice of production can allow us to encounter various problems and enable mass language theory to be further developed. And only the practice of production can prove the correctness or error of the theory. The production of mass language literature is the goal. Simply talking about theory is not enough.

Yesterday, an old friend said to me: "During the 'May Fourth' era, we opposed classical Chinese and advocated vernacular Chinese, and the articles opposing classical Chinese were written in vernacular Chinese. However, now the promoters of mass language advocate mass language, but no one is writing in mass language." I think this is a sincere piece of advice to the promoters of mass language.

In the discussion of the mass language issue, the most important thing is to bring out the works of mass language. And the discussion articles should preferably be written in mass language. It is necessary to bring out the model of mass language text. "Success has always come from experimentation." Only the experimental practice of production can make mass language writing successful.

Just Treat the Joke as a Joke (Part Two) 184

— Kang Bodu

Another strong force attacking vernacular Chinese is Mr. Lin Yutang. What he attacks is not the "difficult to understand" vernacular Chinese, but the "Luli Lusu" vernacular Chinese. He does not even have the idea of Mr. Liu wanting vernacular Chinese to "return to simplicity and truth." To express meaning, only the "analects style" (vernacular Chinese of classical Chinese) will do.

When Mr. Lin appeared armed with vernacular Chinese, the struggle between classical Chinese and vernacular Chinese had already passed. Unlike Mr. Liu, who is a survivor of the melee, he inevitably has a sense of nostalgia and laments the decline of the genre. It is very natural for him to flash and place the Song and Ming Analects under the banner of "humor."

This "humor" is the "How to Write a Note" in the 45th issue of "The Analects." Because he wanted to ask a carpenter for some putty, he wrote a note in the analects style, but he was afraid that others would say that he "opposed vernacular Chinese," so he rewrote it in vernacular Chinese, selected style, and Tongcheng school, but all were ridiculous. In the end, he asked the "pageboy" to pass the message and asked the carpenter for putty.

"The Analects" is a popular publication, so I will not bother to copy it here. In short, the only one that is not ridiculous is the analects style one. The other three are all unacceptable. But the replacement of these four different roles is actually played by Mr. Lin himself. One is the leading man, which is the "analects style," and the other three are clowns who make faces and act strangely, making the leading man look extraordinary.

But this is no longer "humor," but "jesting," which is no different from the street tactics of drawing a turtle on the wall and writing the name of the person he hates on its back. However, those who see it often laugh at the person who is drawn without asking right or wrong.

"Humor" or "jesting" must produce results, unless you know what it means and just treat it as a "joke."

Because the facts may not be as good as the article. For example, this analects-style note has never been completely cut off in China. If you have time, you might as well go to the alleys of Shanghai. Sometimes you will see a stall with a scholar sitting there, writing letters for male and female workers. The writing he uses is definitely not as easy to understand as the note drafted by Mr. Lin, but it is clearly "analects style." This is the end of the analects school that is being revived now, but no one has painted his nose white.

This is a concrete "humor."

But it is really difficult to appreciate "humor." I once proved the rationality of spanking in China from physiology: if the buttocks were born for excretion or sitting, they would not need to be so big. The soles of the feet should be much smaller, wouldn't they be enough to support the whole body? We don't eat people anymore, and we don't need so much meat. So, it can be seen that it is specially for spanking. Sometimes I tell people, and they generally think it is "humor." But if someone has been spanked, or has been spanked himself, I think the feeling would probably not be like this.

There is no way, when everyone is not comfortable, I am afraid that it will eventually be said that "China has no humor."

How to Write a Note 185

— Cao Juren

Mr. Lin Yutang was installing screens at his home, and the edges were not properly sealed, leaving small gaps. He wanted to write a note to ask for some putty to patch the holes. "At first, he wrote it naturally, which is vernacular Chinese of classical Chinese. Later, he was afraid that people would see it and object, so he changed it to classical Chinese of vernacular Chinese. But then he was afraid that the carpenter would not understand it, which would lose the meaning of 'mass language.' Later, the more he changed it, the more confused he became. He inadvertently wrote a piece of four-six that seemed to make sense but didn't. He felt dissatisfied, so he learned from Han Yu and revived the decline of the Eight Dynasties, writing ancient prose of the Three Dynasties. But he felt that the words 'putty' were not elegant enough, so he gave up halfway." (My Words in the 45th issue of The Analects) This is Mr. Lin's joking style, with the meaning beyond the words, and we understand each other without speaking.

Mr. Lin drafted four kinds of notes. The parallel prose is not satisfactory, and the one learning from Han is also a bit of a donkey. The "classical Chinese of vernacular Chinese" is deliberately written in a twisted and unnatural way. Now let's discuss what Mr. Lin calls the "natural writing method." Mr. Lin's original note is as follows: "XX Baohao. The screen you installed the other day has gaps along the edges, so mosquitoes can get in. Catch one when it comes, and another comes again, making it impossible to sit during the day and sleep at night, which is very painful. I am sending someone to ask for a little putty to repair it. I hope you will not value putty and take credit lightly. XX Qizhi"

In my opinion, this note is not a natural writing method. The purpose of this note is to get a little putty. You don't need to say any reason, or even if you want to say a reason, it is enough to say that there are gaps in the window edges. The issue of mosquitoes coming in and out does not seem to need to be mentioned. (If this note were written to a lover, that would be another matter. Perhaps the lover would feel a little distressed after seeing the mosquitoes biting and would quickly buy putty and send it over, which is also possible.)

Now, let me try it:

(A) Classical Chinese Style

The screen installed the other day still has cracks along the edges. Send someone to get putty and please give a little. Yours sincerely,

XX BaohaoXXX

(B) Vernacular Style

That day, the screen you installed for me had leaks on the edges. I am sending someone to the store to get some putty. Please wrap a little for him to bring back!

XX BaohaoXXX

Mr. Lin's final solution was to have Ah Jing pass the message verbally. I think Ah Jing must have had the following conversation when he went to the store to ask for putty:

"Ah Jing": Boss, Mr. Lin asked me to get some putty.

Boss: What do you need it for?

Ah Jing: The screen you installed for us the other day had leaks on the edges!

Boss: Clerk! Wrap a little putty and give it to him to take back!"

Okay, my note and what Ah Jing said verbally are consistent. Mr. Lin, let's give up that "vernacular Chinese of classical Chinese" and write honest mass language!

Village Memories 186

— Liu Ming

I once spent a delightful summer in a farmer's house at Sītáng Bridge in Bǎoshān. Now, recalling it, that rural village, encircled by a small river and surrounded by green trees, suddenly brings forth a chorus of cicadas and unfolds before my eyes, as if I have returned to that place of past visits.

That elderly landlord, is he still, at midday, holding a child, dragging his swollen feet afflicted by dampness, slowly walking to the hibiscus hedge, wrinkling his forehead as he gazes for a while at the sun-scorched fields, and then silently returning, sitting under the jujube tree shade, listlessly fanning himself with a cattail fan, allowing flies to leisurely stroll across his face? I hope he is still like that, because in my heart I can't help but think that at his age, with those ailing feet, perhaps during the January 28th Incident, he was hit by a small bullet and fell into the stream.

His wife, a talkative old woman, should still be alive and well, often returning from the cotton fields, her head covered in sweat. As soon as she enters the wicker gate with one or two sunflowers drooping over it, she calls out, and the white chickens and mottled chickens, responding to her call, gather around her like a group of children, stretching their long necks. Her blue cloth apron, which holds something, suddenly opens, and various tender green grasses are scattered on the bodies and necks of the chickens. At the same time, she quickly hides as if escaping something, her eyes swiftly noticing something else.

"Oh dear, the pig has run out again!"

Or:

"How can you dry things like that? The clothes have been blown onto the muddy ground."

Whenever she comes back, the house and veranda are filled with her energetic voice. Sitting by the window reading or writing, I am often tempted to look up and walk out of the quiet and leisurely little house to share her joy in busyness. Because when one is idle, one envies those who are working.

Every day, when I tire of reading, I stand up, stretch my waist, and raise my wrists. The green cotton fields dotted with women in white headscarves, beyond the fence, come to the window along with the clear breeze. If her two sons were also working in the cotton fields, I would have thrown my books on the table, kicked off my wooden clogs in the corner, and run barefoot to weed with them. Because in the fields there were also her young daughter-in-law and daughter, who, in a Chinese society like this, should be avoided.

Her two sons never went to the cotton fields to weed (as if weeding was something only women did). They only did other things, sometimes sleeping for half a day, and after waking up, they would lazily sit on the earthen steps, twisting their mouths and leisurely smoking cigarettes. At first, seeing the women so busy, sweating under the scorching sun, and then having to come home to cook and take care of the children while eating, I simply felt disgusted with them: why are men so lazy? Later, bothered by the swarms of mosquitoes, I went to the fields at night and found them working hard night fishing by the receding river. Then I felt deeply ashamed, because in the village, the truly lazy one, I should admit, was myself.

The Art of Name-Spreading 187

— Dūn Páng

Anecdotes from the Literary World of the Qing Dynasty, No. 5

Chá Xiàzhòng, Jiāng Xīmíng, Táng Dōngjiāng, Tāng Xīyá, Gōng Shùtáng, Shǐ Jiāoyǐn, gathered in the capital for literary and wine gatherings. They once said that if each of them published their own collections in the future, whether they would be remembered or not was uncertain. The only way to ensure remembrance was to weave each other's names into their collections. A hundred years later, if one of them was remembered, all would be remembered. This is how scholars, with their fondness for fame, clung to their habits.

Note: Scholars have a fondness for fame, and there are many ways to seek it. However, rather than writing an autobiography or recording how many times one played cards or drank with Ms. Lú Yǐn, or using a pseudonym to write a critique praising one's own novels, it is better to find a way to weave one's name into the writings of others. An autobiography is good, but it may not be remembered. Articles about Lú Yǐn and critiques by pseudonymous critics may also not be remembered. But if a writer who is likely to be remembered is willing to include my name in his writings, then even if I am criticized, my name will certainly be passed down. Therefore, recently, a writer published an open letter in his publication to another writer, provoking him, but in the end said, "If the gentleman feels this letter is worth responding to, please send it to the editor at XXXXX for publication. Otherwise, I hope the gentleman will write a serious critique of me. I think any publication would welcome it."

Further Note: When I read "Qing Dynasty Unofficial History Grand View," I always note that it was borrowed from Mr. Cáo Jùrén, also to give Mr. Cáo another chance to be remembered, if my writing can be remembered. But I wonder if Mr. Cáo would be willing to mention my humble name in his articles, saying that he once lent me books?

I Come From the East (7) 188

— Xīngyě

West of Rocky Mountain, all that passed were beautiful fields. Within the Columbia River basin, the wheat fields are comparable to the Snake River basin in the western United States. What impressed and admired me most here was their irrigation system. For example, the hometown of Senator Borah, Boise City, was originally barren land, but now the man-made canals have encircled this small city. Green grass grows on both sides of the canals, covering the ground peacefully like a carpet. To call this a city is not as accurate as calling it an extremely hygienic park. Who would know that before irrigation, this place was a desolate, yellow wasteland? I admire the greatness of material science because it has allowed mankind to have such beautiful places. Great material science, it can create heaven for mankind from hell.

Creating heaven from hell is the continuous pursuit of progressive peoples. In terms of material construction, Americans certainly have this ability and spirit. The American West was developed later, but many construction projects have already surpassed the older East. They have maintained the courage, adventurousness, and recklessness left by the Red Indians, accumulated more than a hundred years of hard work and endurance, and used the latest scientific inventions to transform their material environment. I envy them, I am jealous of them, and I hope that the Chinese nation on the other side of the Pacific also has the same spirit and the same effort!

Canada—England? America?

Five days of driving took me from the Atlantic coast in the far east of the United States to the Pacific coast in the far west. On a rainy morning, I arrived in Seattle, which I had not seen for three years. That is the northwesternmost corner of the United States. A journey of more than three thousand miles had disappeared behind my feet. I saw the Pacific Ocean, looking west in the setting sun toward what I usually thought was where the sun set. It seemed that my motherland was not far away. I seemed to see the shadows of the mountains and fields of China on the opposite horizon.

In this corner of the Pacific, three large cities are cleverly arranged. If the Pacific is the night sky, they are three stars in the sky. Seattle is the one to the south, across the Strait of Georgia to the north, the lively Vancouver to the east, and the beautiful Victoria City to the west. Within twenty-four hours a day, trains, planes, and ships are constantly circling between these cities, connecting these three small stars into a ring. The people living inside the ring are closely related in their lives. However, irrational political boundaries have placed these three cities under two different flags.

Ministry of Education Interprets Primary School Regulations 194

The Ministry recently clarified two matters regarding the interpretation of elementary school regulations. (1) According to the Education Department of Shanxi Province, Article 101 of the Elementary School Regulations states that each province may designate provincial elementary schools or provincial normal schools affiliated with elementary schools within the provincial district as the central elementary school of the district. The term "district" in "provincial district" refers to whether a county is a district, or whether several counties are a district, and whether the entire province can be divided into several districts. The instruction to the department was that the term "district" in "provincial district" refers to several counties. As for how many districts the entire province should be divided into, the department should determine the number of districts based on the actual situation of school establishment in the province and convenience of research. (2) According to the Education Department of Gansu Province, an interpretation of Article 4 of the Elementary School Law and Article 11 of the Elementary School Regulations was requested (it is easy to regulate the names of elementary schools in townships, but the areas within the county seats of Gansu are smaller, and the place names are no more than a certain street or alley, which is far less complicated than the names in the county seats of the southeastern provinces. If public elementary schools below the county and city level are named after place names in smaller areas without adding the word "county seat", it seems that you are explicit. Take an example, such as the location of the No. 1 Elementary School in Gaolan County, now the No. 1 District of Caojia Lane in Gaolan County, and the funding is from the county government. According to the above sections, what should the school name be to be appropriate? ). The instruction to the department was that, according to Article 11 of the Elementary School Regulations, which stipulates that public elementary schools below the county and city level should be named after place names in smaller areas, the No. 1 Elementary School in Gaolan County should be renamed as Caojia Lane Elementary School, Gaolan County. Other county town area elementary schools that need to be renamed in similar situations should also be renamed by analogy.

Breeze Literary Society Condemns Lǔ Xùn and Lín Yǔtáng 195

First Meeting Held Yesterday

Shanghai News: The Breeze Literary Society held its first meeting yesterday. Attendees included Zhū Shàngchūn, Méi Zi, Tóng Chìmín, Lài Zǐwén, Sū Bànglián, Gāo Wánbái, Huáng Jìngchǎng, Chén Dōngbái, Zhū Zhìwū, Wú Shíjùn, Xíng Huìmín, Yóu Qízhī, and others, more than ten in total. Zhū Xiǎochūn chaired the meeting, and Tóng Chìmín recorded the minutes. Matters discussed: (1) How to handle the proposal to condemn Lǔ Xùn and Lín Yǔtáng submitted by the general meeting? It was resolved: (A) A public telegram will be issued, drafted by Méi Zi, Gāo Wánbái, and Tóng Chìmín. (B) A letter will be sent to the publishing industry in China requesting that they refuse to publish the works of Lǔ Xùn and Lín Yǔtáng until their style changes. (C) A letter will be sent to the national press requesting that they universally refuse to publish the works and advertisements of Lǔ Xùn and Lín Yǔtáng until their style changes. (D) A request will be submitted to Party and government agencies to severely punish the two literary demons, Lǔ Xùn and Lín Yǔtáng. (E) Lǔ Xùn and Lín Yǔtáng will be warned to quickly change their style, otherwise, they will be fought to the end. (2) How to unite young writers across the country to launch a total attack on Proletarian decadent literature? It was resolved: (A) A telegram will be sent to the literary circles across the country to launch a unified attack. (B) A request will be submitted to the Central Propaganda Department and Party and government agencies in various regions to severely ban it. (C) A letter will be sent to the publishing industry across the country to universally refuse to publish works of Proletarian decadent literature. (3) Publication of journals? It was resolved to be jointly planned by the General Affairs and Publishing Departments. (4) Broadcasts and speeches? It was resolved to be planned and implemented by the Affairs Department. (5) Tasking someone to draft the theory and policy of new literature? It was resolved to task Xíng Huìmín, Gāo Wánbái, and Méi Zi to be responsible for drafting. (6) The drama department proposed organizing a spoken drama broadcasting troupe? It was resolved to task Sū Chūnlián to be responsible for preparation. Other proposals were omitted.

Jiangsu Department of Education Formulates Provisional Regulations for Middle School Performance Exhibitions 203

Zhenjiang News: In order to enhance the effectiveness of secondary school education, the Jiangsu Department of Education ordered all provincial middle schools to hold a performance exhibition once before the end of each semester, and stipulated the provisional measures for holding performance exhibitions in secondary schools in Jiangsu Province, which are disclosed below.

Article 1. These measures are specially formulated by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education in order to enhance the effectiveness of secondary school education. Article 2. The achievements to be exhibited by each school are divided into three categories: administrative achievements, teaching achievements, and student achievements. (1) Administrative achievements include: records of major school events, important work records, records of various meetings, various assessment records, administrative records, financial receipts and disbursements, various accounts and vouchers and statistics, school building and teaching aid catalogs, library instrument catalogs, school building and teaching aid repair and purchase statistics, enrollment statistics, graduate employment statistics, various statistics on students in school, statistics on physical education and health, and other statistics, records, and research related to school administration. (2) Teaching achievements include: teaching records, classroom diaries, tutor work records, teaching outlines, teaching records, teacher absence and make-up class statistics, student grade reports, student academic records, records of student absences, requests for leave, statistics on illnesses, textbooks for each level and subject, self-compiled and printed teaching materials for each subject, teacher research works, and other statistics, records, and research related to teaching. (3) Student achievements include: works of all students, such as composition books, notebooks, reading notes, exercise books, internship reports, visit reports, teaching plans, calligraphy paintings, labor practice books or works, extracurricular reading notebooks, life weekly or daily journals, specimens, models, instrument collections and manufactures, extracurricular research, works of extracurricular assignments, regular and semester examination papers for each subject, and all other student works. Article 3. Each school shall hold a performance exhibition once before the end of each semester, and shall indicate the exhibition date in the school calendar at the beginning of the semester and report it to the Education Department for record. The exhibition period shall be no more than three days. Article 4. The performance exhibition of each school must display all the achievements accumulated over time, and must not be rushed to produce temporarily. All daily school records and teacher evaluations of student works must be signed or stamped by the person in charge at any time, and the date must be indicated. The date, the name and class of the producer, and the name of the instructor must also be marked on each product. Article 5. When each school holds a performance exhibition, the exhibited achievements must be arranged in order, classified, and graded according to the items stipulated in Article 2. The classification must be clearly marked, and a general catalog must be compiled for reference. The number of student works must be compared with the number of students in each level in a list. Article 6. During the exhibition period, in addition to inviting students' parents, social figures, and principals and teachers of schools of the same level to comment, the school's faculty and staff should jointly study matters for improvement, and the principal should carefully examine them, formulate award and punishment measures and improvement plans, and report them to the Education Department for verification. The Education Department may send personnel to inspect at any time. Article 7. In addition to each school holding a performance exhibition, the Education Department may conduct a joint exhibition by sampling one or several achievements. Article 8. These measures shall be formulated and implemented by the Jiangsu Education Department, and shall be reported to the Ministry of Education and the Provincial Government for record.

Jiangsu Social Education Agency Vacation Measures 204

The Jiangsu Department of Education previously instructed the Social Education Agency to present the vacation measures for social education agencies for verification (there are no clear regulations on whether social education agencies have winter and summer vacations, and whether Sundays and holidays are off on the day or compensated on the next day). It was instructed by the Ministry of Education to check the vacation of social education agencies and should follow the following regulations: 1. They may take turns to rest in severe cold and hot weather, but they may not take vacations. The dates shall be determined separately by the educational administrative agencies of each province and city and national social education agencies according to local conditions, and reported to the Ministry of Education for record. 2. No vacations on Sundays and holidays, all compensated on the next day. 3. No vacations during the New Year, compensated from January 4th to 6th, etc. The order has been communicated for compliance.

Shen Bao National Goods Weekly

A Contribution

The Spirit of Loving National Goods 229

— Yang An

I once said: "The degree to which people love national goods is less in large commercial ports than in inland cities, and even less in inland cities than in poor and remote rural areas." My trip to Nanchang this time has made me even more convinced that this statement is not wrong. Nanchang is an inland city, with transportation from Jiujiang via the Nanxun Railway, which can be reached in half a day. Motor vehicles on highways are even more accessible in all directions. Since the Unofficial Transport Commission and Chairman Chiang’s camp stationed there recently, vigorously carrying out the New Life Movement and actively advocating a simple life, the people of Nanchang are all striving to use domestic products. Recently, the sales of foreign goods have been decreasing day by day. Taking foreign piece goods as an example, the annual sales were one million yuan three years ago, but now it is less than two million yuan. In addition, the sales of imported goods, according to Jiangxi merchants, account for only one-third of what they were two or three years ago. In the future, as the effects of the New Life Movement increase day by day, the sales of foreign goods will decrease day by day. This news is truly gratifying. After I arrived in Nanchang, I talked with Mr. Cai Shenzhai, the president of the Bank of China, and learned that the Nanchang business community now has a kind of ambition: to sell domestic products as much as possible whenever domestic products can be used. This spirit of courageously loving the country and being happy to sacrifice is even more worthy of emulation by Shanghai merchants. I also had the honor of being introduced by Mr. Cai to talk with various business leaders. Everyone expressed good feelings about the great progress made by Shanghai's national goods factories in recent years, and they are extremely willing to do their best to promote and cooperate with each other. At present, they plan to organize a national goods company to cooperate with the Shanghai production industry in actual production and sales. In the near future, it will not be difficult to realize a purely Chinese national goods company. Those who join are all leaders in the financial and industrial and commercial circles, as well as well-established merchants, and they have even gained local trust. This spirit of loving national goods is truly worthy of praise and admiration.

Talks on National Loans

Foreign Goods Lead to National Ruin 230

— Yiyi Mansion Owner

To say that "foreign goods lead to national ruin," we must first talk about "national goods saving the country."

We know that "national goods saving the country" has been shouted for a long time. However, to this day, the "foreign goods" on the market are still everywhere. The effectiveness of "national goods saving the country" is really equal to zero! Although people of insight designated last year as "National Goods Year" and this year as "Women's National Goods Year," the "National Goods Year" of last year resulted in a complete mess. As for this year's "Women's National Goods Year," twelve months have already passed six months. In these six months, how has "national goods saving the country" performed? According to the newspapers, it is: "Imports exceed exports" are increasing without decrease, especially the "cosmetics" needed by women every day, the amount is astonishing! Alas! In this situation, I feel that it is better to say frankly and honestly, "foreign goods lead to national ruin," rather than saying "national goods save the country" and just making foreigners laugh.

Or, it may be said: "National goods saving the country" is, in fact, the opposite of "foreign goods leading to national ruin." Because "foreign goods" can "lead to national ruin," that's why we need "national goods" to "save the country."

I say, "Although what you say is not bad, on the one hand, we keep shouting 'national goods saving the country,' while on the other hand, we keep maintaining an inextricable relationship with 'foreign goods.' If this contradictory strange phenomenon continues without reform, then there will eventually be a day of national ruin! May I ask, will this kind of national ruin be 'national goods saving the country,' or will it be 'foreign goods leading to national ruin?'"

Stores Should Use National Goods for Gifts Across the Board 231

— Chu Jianping

Using gifts to compete for business is indeed a very effective and harmless method in business ethics. However, at a time when the whole country is shouting itself hoarse and calling for the promotion of national goods, everyone should use complete national goods as gifts across the board. Otherwise, it will inevitably lead to criticism and ridicule.

Recently, a certain silk store, in order to give preferential treatment to its customers, gave away XX brand orange soda from X country. This was originally nothing to be surprised about, but I don't know why they had to abandon the cheap and high-quality domestic products and willingly pay a very expensive price to expand business and widely promote for foreign merchants? Is it possible that there are no high-quality orange sodas among domestic products?

Originally, China has suffered to the point where no citizen can tolerate harboring jealousy anymore; and the industrial and commercial circles should especially work together with one heart and one mind, complementing each other. The price of goods supplied by manufacturers to stores as gifts should be even cheaper than ordinary wholesale prices; because stores are directly attracting their own customers, and indirectly they are helping the manufacturers of the gifts to spread the effect of advertising.

Alas! Honest managers! The situation no longer allows you to sit idly by. Hurry up and cooperate!

Alas! In short, I hope that this year's "Women's National Goods Year" will not be as bad as last year's "National Goods Year"! I urge everyone to work hard and promote "national goods" to overthrow "foreign goods," so that "foreign goods leading to national ruin" will not really become a reality. That would truly be an immeasurable good deed!

It is Especially Appropriate to Promote National Goods in Cities 232

— Rong Yu

Promoting national goods has been noisy for quite some time. Is it effective? The customs statistics show that foreign goods are constantly increasing. Is it ineffective? Several national goods companies' business is not declining, which is confusing. In fact, people who love national goods have become a little more enthusiastic because of the promotion. As for some people who are still desperately promoting foreign goods, no matter how much you talk until your tongue is parched and your lips are dry, they remain unmoved. I can use a literary saying to describe these people: "Shu Bao has no conscience at all." Now there are many people who advocate promoting national goods, starting with the countryside first. That's right! I also thought of this point. Because the area of ​​the entire China is mostly rural. As long as all national goods are used in the countryside, even if foreign goods are still used in the bustling cities, the number will be limited. More than ten years ago, I followed a few enthusiastic gentlemen and brought many domestic goods to the inland areas to travel and persuade people. Many villagers only bought a little after listening to your persuasion. They were perfunctory to your face; it can also be said that they bought some cheap goods because they were half-given and half-sold, so the result was a failure. Because of this, my thinking changed. Promoting in the countryside is indeed necessary, but the heavier work should be applied to the cities, because what is loved in the cities will be imitated by the towns and villages. "The city girls wear high buns, and the countryside follows suit by one foot." This sentence is really true.

The three things that people cannot live without are of course "clothing," "food," and "use." First, let's take the clothes people wear: people in Europe and America take the styles of Paris as the standard. Whatever is fashionable in Paris, other places will follow and imitate. In China, of course, it is Shanghai. What is popular in Shanghai gradually spreads to Suzhou and Hangzhou, and even to remote rural areas. If the fashionable women in the city, no matter how new the patterns are, use domestic fabrics, the people in the inland and rural areas will not need to be persuaded at this time, they will naturally follow the trend. In addition, what about the food and things people use? Isn't it all the same?

People in the cities! You are the teachers and role models for the people of the whole country. If you love national goods, the people of the whole country will also rise up and love them. If you love foreign goods and insist that the people in the inland areas only use national goods, that is impossible, and it is also unreasonable!

The Shamelessness of Unscrupulous Merchants 233

— Shi Ying

National Goods Sigh

More on the National Goods Showcase Competition 234

— Qian Hong

Before criticizing this Chenshe display of the Peide Tie Company, please first talk about the two methods of showing neckties.

The narrow neckties are placed in the entire showcase, requiring beauty that can attract the eye; they must be gathered together. After gathering, it is more stimulating, it can attract the line of sight of people who pass by where it is placed. It can attract the advertiser's harvest advertising effect. So the design of showcasing neckties is originally not easy. If you use pure straight lines or the two-pronged method of straight and curved lines to display neckties, it seems more likely to succeed.

In the showcase of the National Goods Display Showcase Competition held by the Huamei Tobacco Company, the Peide Tie Company does not seem to have noticed the wonderful patterns that can be formed from the neckties themselves, nor did they notice the combination of colors and patterns. This is really a very pity. Their showcase focuses on the amount and trademarks, so the concentration of stimulation depends entirely on the two neckties hanging under the heads of the two Western movie stars, Laurel and Hardy, as the main body of the entire showcase. Of course, the funny portraits, although only two heads, I think are also very unique and easy to attract attention. Their registered trademark is a black cat, in the posture of playing the zither, the humorous meaning is even stronger.

Because they focus on the amount, the display of various patterns of neckties is almost full. In terms of color, light colors are the main body, because it is now the hot summer.

Finally, Huamei Tobacco Company's own window decorations this time are very magnificent. They use the colors of green, yellow, blue, and red silk to represent their four kinds of cigarettes. At night, the light shines in all directions, which is indeed very stimulating. Which of the two is better depends entirely on the individual's point of view.

Commercial News

The Rise in Financial Silver is Not Enough to Affect the Standard Gold 235

Supply and Demand Both Stand in Equilibrium

Half-Day Process Continues to Show Hesitant Climate

Yesterday's gold market saw that although the silver market has rebounded, the increase is not much, and people's minds have not been hit, but are relatively stable. It is estimated that private telegrams are still shrinking, and the market situation in the first half of the day is still weak after the initial firmness, with a mediocre situation. Initially, overseas silver markets rose in the UK and remained flat in the US, and the futures silver price of the Metals Exchange rose by 0.22 to 0.37 cents. The exchange rate was flat, the price of London raw gold rose by half a penny, US wheat shrank by 0.2 cents, US cotton fell by 24 pounds per quintal, stocks fell slightly, and the prices of goods opened flat. Preliminary transactions opened slightly stable. Yuqing Yongfuxing Yongyongli and others bought one after another, rising to 92.3 yuan. After the opening, although buyers surged, the banks' appetite tended to be full, and sellers were also active, rising high and falling again. The HSBC exchange rate remained unchanged, the market was quite flat, and the fluctuations were also narrow. In the end, due to the slight loosening of the foreign exchange market, the banks continued to supply, and people's minds have also turned weak, gradually falling downstream. However, the supply and demand in the field are balanced, and the gold market is still hovering. Later, the Seattle night market silver price reported a rise of 0.1 to 0.5 points and 1.375. People's minds were originally timid, so a selling trend started, once breaking the 90 yuan mark. However, the falling trend was weak, because the Seattle night market silver price was not noticed by general major investors. The industry still had the intention of cutting prices, resulting in a peaceful domestic market. Many buyers took advantage of the low price, and the gold price gradually rose. The situation at noon was very stable, because the Seattle night market silver price had reports of non-movement and shrinking by 0.25, and the silver market trend was observed to be unlikely to rise again, and people's minds were still good, and the shorts had slightly closed their positions. The swap situation was stable, with a discount of about 3.5 yuan. The spot market situation was calm. Today, the market situation in the first half of the day will be recorded later.

Securities "Nine-Six" Reorganization Clearly Disappoints 239

Ministry of Finance Reply Offers No Solution

Long Positions Unload, Price Plunges Over One Yuan

Yesterday, the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange experienced a significant turmoil regarding the "Nine-Six" securities. Initially, there was some hope for reorganization. However, news arrived from the north that the Ministry of Finance had replied, stating that it was impossible to reorganize "Nine-Six." Long positions, losing all hope, rushed to unload their holdings, fearing they would be unable to sell. The market price plummeted sharply. As the situation became clear and many long positions sought to sell, the downward trend is likely to intensify. The price had been driven too high previously due to the reorganization rumors, and now, without reorganization, the fall is bound to be even more severe. The difference between the high and low prices, within just two weeks, was as much as ten yuan, demonstrating the danger of speculation. Other securities could have seen price increases, but due to the sharp fall of "Nine-Six," market sentiment turned negative, and they also weakened in tandem. In reality, "Nine-Six" has no principal or interest and has always been separate and independent, with no connection to other securities. Yesterday, at the opening, various bonds saw slight increases of 0.2 to 0.3 yuan. However, "Nine-Six" bucked the trend, falling from high to low, dropping by 0.45 yuan. As news of the Ministry of Finance's reply gradually spread, "Nine-Six" plummeted by 0.9 yuan, and other securities also fell by small amounts, from 0.2 to 0.5 yuan. The final results showed mixed performance. Securities listed earlier were slightly better by 0.2 to 0.3 yuan, while those closed off were slightly lower by 0.1 to 0.2 yuan. When quoting prices, foreign wheat prices fell by 0.5, 0.6, and 0.7 yuan respectively. After the second trade, northern merchants aggressively bought, flipping from short to long. The near month also formed a squeeze due to delivery, which led to large purchases in the distant months, and prices rose rapidly. Although the major factories tried their best to sell during each trade, the situation was out of control, and their efforts were in vain. The only way to solve the problem is to eliminate the foreign wheat tax and relieve the tension. (North Shanghai) Eight or nine sources of goods arrived from the Hexia area yesterday. Sales on the market are still sluggish. High-quality japonica rice is down about 0.2 yuan, and medium-quality and second-rate rice are down 0.3 to 0.4 yuan. Thin rice is the same. Early rice and Yang Du Jian are down 0.2 to 0.3 yuan. Bai Yuan is a little smaller than expected.

Yellow Soybeans Sell Well 253

Yesterday, New Town Gate soybeans from Jiujiang continued to fall by a fraction, with prices opening at 3.55 to 3.4 yuan. More than 300 bags were traded, all of which were leftover goods from the previous day. The destination was still the Ningbo and local merchants. There were 500 to 600 bags remaining unstored. Currently, market sentiment is that the high-priced goods will decline only slightly, so the future situation may be stable. There are no new soybeans from Hankou available. The market for old soybeans is high and stable, as the supply of high-quality goods is decreasing. As a result, factory warehouses of second-grade goods are active, and market prices continue to rise. Yesterday, a train of Zhengyangguan soybeans was unloaded, priced at 5.24 to 5.2 yuan, and two trains of Feihe soybeans were priced at 3.16 to 3.1 yuan, all of which were sold in this area. American Sales of Chinese Silk Remain Weak: The sluggishness of American sales of Chinese silk has reached an extreme. Yesterday, the New York class Taiyi wheel left without any silk shipped to the United States. The future of American sales is exceptionally bleak.

Gangmen Seizes Cheap Opportunities to Purchase Factory Yarn: Overseas raw silk prices are gradually falling, and silk sales are sluggish, with little prospect of a turnaround in the near future. 御香縹緲錄 260

— Original by Princess Der Ling of Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Sometimes, if she really felt like she had nothing to do, she would occasionally play solitaire. We would stand behind her, keeping a close watch for her. If she made a mistake, we would point it out. Also, if she needed glasses, a pipe, or other small items, and these items were nearby and easily within reach, we would go and get them for her. However, if these items were far away and required more effort to retrieve, we would let the palace maids handle it. In short, the palace maids were responsible for the more strenuous tasks, while we, as female officials, could disregard them.

Please forgive my boldness in saying something boastful: although we eight female officials had different personalities, we all had very attractive appearances. Perhaps this goes without saying, but it isn't far from the truth, so I'll just say it directly! We all wore the same headdresses, but we were careful to avoid uniformity in our clothing. Not only did we avoid imitating each other's styles, but we also ensured that the colors of our clothes didn't clash. For example, if someone wore a light red dress one day, the other seven would not wear that color. So when the eight of us stood together, onlookers couldn't help but praise our beauty; even we ourselves felt pleased, especially since we were all young and, once dressed up, each of us looked extremely beautiful!

Every night, after the Empress Dowager had fallen asleep, one of us had to attend to her in her bedroom. Because this was a more tiring task, we took turns being on duty. Each of us was on duty once every seven days, and we didn't find it too difficult. However, before the Empress Dowager fell asleep, the person attending to her had to talk to her casually until she started snoring loudly. Fortunately, this didn't take too long, so everyone could manage. Even more fortunately, she never suffered from insomnia, or it would have been terrible! (91)

申報's Elder Brother 261

— Yan Qiao

Of all the newspapers printed in Chinese characters that still exist today, everyone considers 申報 to be the eldest brother.

Because it is already sixty-two years old this year. However, Mr. Cheng Zhanlu told me that there is also a "Circulation Daily" in Hong Kong, which held its seventieth anniversary celebration last year and printed a commemorative album with a photo of the founder, Wang Tao, on it. So it is nine years older than 申報, and should be called the eldest brother. Because it is not sold in the mainland, everyone is unaware of it.

According to the Nanjing court gazette, Macau was the first place to publish Chinese newspapers, probably during the Daoguang and Xianfeng periods. Unfortunately, they were all short-lived. Due to cultural backwardness and the shift of commercial centers, there were no successors, so everyone has lost even the historical impression of this.

Speaking of newspapers in China, there were two types in the Tang Dynasty: "Miscellaneous Reports" and "Di Reports." The former was found in Sun Kezhi's collected works, and the latter was found in the Complete Tang Tales. It is unknown whether the Miscellaneous Reports are the same as the Di Reports, but their content can be inferred to be similar to the Qing Dynasty's Palace Gate Copies. The Palace Gate Copies were copied from the Inner Cabinet and printed using woodblocks. They were distributed to Beijing officials every evening, and the delivery person was paid four strings of cash per month. Later, with the advent of news newspapers, vendors could be entrusted with delivery, and two strings of cash per month were enough. The content was only the imperial edicts announced that day and the names of officials summoned, as well as the names of important provincial officials arriving in Beijing, which was not very meaningful.

"Qiu Shui Sheng's Textual Research" cites Zhao Shu's "Essentials of Court and Wildness," which states that "The court gazette is compiled by the Later Province every day, and those called 'Inner Probes,' 'Provincial Probes,' and 'Yamen Probes' are all private small reports, and there is a prohibition against leakage, so they are secretly called 'News.'" It is unknown what political organization the Later Province is. "Probes" are very similar to today's "reporters." In my childhood, I saw people selling small, leaflet-like news newspapers called "court gazettes" while banging small gongs. They had the same name but different content from the court gazettes mentioned in the "Essentials of Court and Wildness," or perhaps they were imitations compiled and printed by the people, and they contained social news, which was very much in line with the meaning of "private small reports."

The Omen of Assemblies 262

— Mei Xue

"Assembly" is a common word in Suzhou people's vocabulary, they always say it several times a day. "Assembly today," "assembly tomorrow," "evening assembly," "meeting assembly," everyone says it very fluently. Who would have thought that it would be an omen for the severe drought of the year? I was born in the Republican era, and I have certainly enjoyed many material blessings, but parading with idols in processions is something I have never seen. I have only heard elderly people talk about the grand occasions of the "Three Festival Assemblies" in the Qing Dynasty. These dozens of days of drought, though disastrous for the old farmers, have benefited me. What have they benefited me? It is that I have assemblies to watch every day. I watched the assembly today, then watched the assembly tomorrow; watched the evening assembly, then watched the meeting assembly. Who would have thought that for the sake of seeking rain, the clay and wooden sculptures inside and outside Suzhou city would be so active, and I could see this "reverse gear" idol race.

After the Guan Di assembly came the Fierce General assembly. After all, the Fierce General has a big face. After the assembly, there was a drizzle. The devout men and women said, "Guan Di couldn't break into the South Heaven Gate, so seeking rain was ineffective. The Fierce General was once conferred the title of Heavenly King, and he is the Jade Emperor's nephew, so he can directly enter the South Heaven Gate and pester his mother to bring some rain. Therefore, as soon as the Fierce General left the temple, there was a sign of rain in the sky." These superstitious, ghost-seeing words made believers nod their heads, but to me, it was just like setting off firecrackers in the back slaughterhouse.

The Horse King Temple, which is worshiped by grooms, had a grand race a few days ago. All the horses in the city joined the race. The banner of "Horse Bright King" fluttered in the wind, how magnificent! But as I see it, in addition to the Horse King Temple, there are also the Cow King Temple and the Snake King Temple in Suzhou city. If they were made in the same way, a fire cow formation could be arranged in the Cow King assembly, and a long snake formation could be arranged in the Snake King assembly. Furthermore, in Temple Hall Lane, there is a Gecko King Temple. If the Gecko King also came out to seek rain, I'm afraid that all the bedbugs in Suzhou city would have no chance to join.

Emperor Rang and Jiang Taigong came out on the same day. Who is Emperor Rang? He is Wu Taibo, the uncle of King Wen of Zhou. In terms of qualifications, he is certainly above Taigong. The two races met in the middle of the road. In theory, Taigong should yield to Taibo, but Taibo should not yield to Taigong. However, that day, Wu Taibo instead cleared the way, letting Jiang Shang, holding the apricot yellow flag, pass by in a grand manner. This was not appropriate in terms of etiquette. However, the incense burners defended Old Jiang, saying that "Jiang Taigong gets promoted one rank when he meets an official, so he certainly wouldn't give face to Wu Taibo."

— Shi Ying

Four Company Commanders of the Northeast 264

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 32: General Amuses Himself with Pleasures All Day Long; Soldiers Return with Few Amidst Tears from Young and Old

Gui Zhi replied from inside the house: "We wouldn't dare to accept that. Even a concubine is a million times better than us. How could we dare say we're not qualified?" When Jiang heard them arguing, she knew this wasn't the way to go, so she interjected, "In that case, I'll accompany these old sisters for a walk. I'll have a good talk with the concubine, and she'll understand." The old woman just wanted to complete her task so she could reduce her own responsibility, and she didn't necessarily need to bring Gui Zhi along. So she smiled and said, "That's good too. You can come with me." Jiang had prepared a long and well-reasoned speech, planning to both avoid offending the concubine and win her over. She followed the old woman into Commander Quan's mansion, went upstairs, and the old woman asked Jiang to wait in the hallway. She went into a room. From the gate to the hallway upstairs, soldiers guarded every door in this mansion. Especially near the door in the hallway, two soldiers with box cannons hanging from their waists narrowed their eyes and scrutinized people. Jiang couldn't enter, nor did she dare to retreat. After a very long time, the old woman came out with an unpleasant expression. Seeing Jiang, she forced a smile and said, "Our concubine is busy, why don't you go see our commander first." Jiang tugged at her clothes twice, took two steps back, and frowned, "How can I see the commander?" The old woman said, "It's alright, he's very amiable. You can just say a few words to him, and I'll bring you out." Jiang thought that since she had already come this far, it wouldn't do to back down completely. So she straightened her chest slightly, cheered herself up, and followed the old woman into a room. Jiang only felt that she was stepping on something soft, and the room was furnished with smooth, bright things. There was a large and thick low chair, completely made of green velvet. A man in a suit sat there with his legs crossed, a cigarette in his mouth, and an attitude of not caring about people. He only glanced sideways, not even turning his head. (442)

Old Aunt Ah Da 265

— Wei Ji

In our village, Old Aunt Ah Da and her husband were known as a loving couple. But yesterday I walked past Fourth Horse Road and saw her smiling coquettishly at passersby, making a living from her flesh.

Today, a fellow villager, Mr. Liu, visited. He mentioned Old Aunt Ah Da's matter. I specially record it below for the reference of village women in general.

Old Aunt Ah Da's husband was affected by the bankruptcy of the rural economy and had no choice but to tell Old Aunt Ah Da to go to the city to make a living.

One morning, Old Aunt Ah Da bid farewell to her husband and boarded a small boat, heading into the evil furnace.

In the first few months, Old Aunt Ah Da would bring news to her husband whenever there was a convenient boat. Later, the news gradually became less frequent. According to people who sold goods in the city, Old Aunt Ah Da was different from before. But Old Aunt Ah Da's husband didn't believe it.

One day, at noon, Old Aunt Ah Da suddenly brought a man to the countryside. She asked her husband for a divorce. She left that night.

Later, people in the countryside didn't know her whereabouts, nor did they get any news from her.

Yesterday, I saw her making a living from her flesh on Fourth Horse Road. I don't know who harmed her.

Such almsgiving to beggars is indeed a shocking event in society, and there is even a spirit of mutual assistance among the beggars. The Fall of London 271

The ground in London is sinking year by year. It is said that it will sink nine inches in a hundred years, because it is said that the tributary of the Thames River was filled in 10,000 years ago, and all the holes have now dropped sixty to seventy feet. This is clear evidence. If this is true, then will London not sink into the water in a few years?

Trading a Lottery Ticket for a Meal 272

This is really the most unlucky thing! In Vienna, an assistant in a bookstore recently bought a lottery ticket. One day, he went to a restaurant to eat a meal, but forgot to bring money. Unable to think of a way, he gave the lottery ticket to them. Who knew that on the day of the draw, this lottery ticket won the prize, winning a prize of 80,000 Schillings (Austrian currency), equivalent to 2,000 pounds in English currency. The price of this meal can be considered the most expensive. Do you think this person is unlucky? (Huang Yingdai)

申報 Local Supplement
