Revolution Must First Revolutionize the Heart, Political Reform Must First Change Customs 273

— Cen

Yang Yongtai, Secretary-General of the Headquarters, recently gave a speech at the Post-Recovery Training Conference in various districts, saying "Revolution must first revolutionize the heart, political reform must first change customs." The general idea is that the chaos in China is all due to bad people's hearts, so to transform China, we must first transform people's hearts, and to reform politics, we must start by reforming social customs. Therefore, it is necessary for a few people at the top to lead the way in changing customs and thoroughly carry out the work of revolutionizing the heart today. The speech, which was more than 10,000 words long, was well-organized and can be said to be a magnificent work of the present time. The reasoning is so precise that it is beyond the reach of others. In today's state of moral corruption and depressed people's hearts, this may be considered a powerful criticism.

The hearts of the Chinese people today are indeed so bad. Those at the top are greedy, selfish, base, and vulgar, and will do anything. Those at the bottom are busy with petty gains, opportunistic, and obsequious. People in the world hardly know the word "shame." The higher the position, the more shameless they are. As for the common people, they live in hunger and cold every day. It is as difficult for them to eat a full meal as it is to ascend to heaven. Poverty has crushed every common person, and now every common person lives below the hunger and poverty line. The social atmosphere is indeed too bad. Without a thorough transformation, Chinese society will simply be unable to be saved, and the entire Chinese nation will be unable to be liberated. Therefore, reforming Chinese society is indeed very necessary today.

However, I still have a point to make. Revolution must first revolutionize the heart, political reform must first change customs. Where should we start? I think we should start from the upper levels. Because, as I said before, the most shameless and worst people in society are some upper-level people with status, that is, the shameless and corrupt bureaucrats that the Chairman and Mr. Yang Yongtai despise. These corrupt and shameless bureaucrats are the main instigators of the worst atmosphere in China today. To transform the atmosphere and revolutionize the heart, I think we should start with these people, and transform these people. This is the fundamental way. As for the common people, as I said before, they still have difficulty eating a full meal. Greed and shamelessness seem to be out of the question for them. Even if there is, it is only a matter of eating, which does not involve the scope of greed and shamelessness, so it can be ignored. In this way, transforming people's hearts should first start with the upper-level people. This point is undoubtedly true.

Secondly, regarding the problem of the common people. Now the common people are all worried about not having enough to eat. In the case of not having enough to eat, they may not be able to take care of many things like etiquette and law, which is indeed a bit illegal. However, this illegality is entirely due to hunger and is far different from the corruption of bureaucrats. The solution should start from how to ensure that everyone has enough to eat. Simply punishing with laws or killing seems to be useless. Once the problem of eating is solved, other problems can naturally be solved as well. This is a fundamental problem. If this problem is not solved, other opinions may become empty talk.

Revolution must first revolutionize the heart, political reform must first change customs, which is indeed very necessary today. However, how to revolutionize the heart and how to change customs are problems that must be studied first. Problems such as the common people's eating problems do not seem important at first glance, but they are actually extremely important. If you don't have enough to eat, what are you talking about etiquette and morality? So the most important problem is how to first give them enough to eat.

Miscellaneous Essentials 274

— Qing

In the open space, a large group of men and women were gathered around. Enclosed in the circle were a tall, sturdy man and a skinny little partner. The big man was showing his bare arms, his skin was dark brown, and it shined with sweat. Raising his high-pitched voice, he yelled, waving two wooden sticks back and forth in his hands, doing some tricks for people to see. As he yelled, he ran around in the circle. The little partner was beating a gong, and when the man shouted a sentence, he would follow with an echoing sound, and then beat the gong hard. Scattered on the ground were many things, and in the center were a few bowls, covered with a red cloth. This was what was able to make people stop and squeeze in to take a look. At the same time, they themselves were the only conservators of the secret. They first yelled desperately and beat the gong desperately. The purpose was nothing more than to attract more viewers and get more effects. Because, although there were many tricks, there were actually limited tricks, and they couldn't easily perform one after another. But the interest of the people watching was very fleeting. They were attracted by the loud yelling and gong sound to join in the fun, but it was only a momentary impulse of curiosity. At a glance, they saw that the two, one big and one small, had been fooling around for a long time, but hadn't done anything yet. The enthusiasm gradually disappeared. Moreover, everyone knows that it is a deceptive business. It's just curiosity, so they are also willing to be deceived for a while. However, the magicians never considered this. The man shouted for a while, then stopped shouting. Instead, he changed his posture, suddenly frowning and looking at the people around with a sad face, saying, "Sir, please do a good deed and give a few copper coins. We haven't had anything to eat or drink all day. Give a few copper coins, and we'll perform a magic trick right away." As he spoke, he pointed to the cloth on the ground.

But the shadow of a copper coin was nowhere to be seen. They hoped that everyone would first give copper coins and then do magic tricks, while the people standing were still considering whether to give, depending on how the magic trick was performed. Seeing this situation, the man's face became even more gloomy. He sighed in front of the crowd. Then, he forced a smile and did the same thing again, muttering words in his mouth.

Page 22

He waved the stick and ran around. The little partner beat the gong, but his expression was not as active as before.

This continued for a long time. At one point, they stopped again, stopped shouting, stretched out their hands to ask people for copper coins, almost four or five times. But the magic trick was never performed. Invisibly, they had completely cooled the little interest that everyone had in their hearts. They gradually went from disappointment to anger and disgust. Some people walked away cursing. More and more people walked away. The man looked even more anxious. He kept beating his chest and begging bitterly, "Masters, please do a good deed and give a few copper coins." After he said it himself, he told his little partner to kneel down and beg with him. In the end, the big man himself simply knelt on both knees. But still, no one dropped any copper coins, and instead, it caused a cold sneer. Everyone had the same feeling: they came to see magic tricks, not to see beggars perform.

So the begging begged, and the people walked away. The sound of begging did not disappear until all the people had dispersed. But it flowed to another place.

Lengthy Nonsense 275

— Beggar of Words

"Doctor," as the name suggests, naturally makes patients live, but most of them make patients die.

"Hanging the pot to help the world" doctors were originally supposed to save people, but "hanging the pot to help the county" doctors, who became professional doctors, do not want to save people.

There are Western doctors who came from pharmacy boys, and there are Chinese doctors who do not understand pulse diagnosis or the properties of medicine. It is no wonder that many people die from illness.

Please call a doctor to pay a registration fee and a consultation fee, and enter the hospital to pay a room fee. Nine out of ten poor people die when they get sick.

Poor people have to wait for money to activate their lives, but the lives of rich people are often harmed by money.

There are barbers who cannot cut their own hair, so there is a good reason to say that there are also doctors who cannot cure their own diseases.

If doctors had to pay with their lives for the people they killed, I wonder if anyone would dare to be a doctor?

Doctors who kill patients and still don't understand what disease it was, but cure one patient, talk about their medical principles with exceptional precision.

There are no executioners who cannot kill people, therefore there are no doctors who cannot kill people.

Some doctors kill incurable patients quickly, while others prolong their suffering for a few more days. Doctors who kill them quickly are scolded, while doctors who prolong their suffering become famous.

One Day 276

— Tao

Opening my eyes and then closing them again, soon opening them once more, tossing and turning in bed like this. Having been awake for a long time, naturally, I wouldn't fall back asleep. I was merely using this method to pass the time until my stomach growled unbearably, forcing me to finally get out of bed. By then, the sun was high in the mid-sky, almost noon. Searching everywhere, all my possessions weren't even worth ten cents. How would I manage today?

Borrow some money! There was no other way. Everything that could be pawned had already been pawned. If I didn't take this path, was I really supposed to go hungry? But just thinking about the faces of those wealthy people sent a chill down my spine. Still, I had to bite the bullet and give it a try!

I hurriedly wiped my face and ran out.

Under the scorching June sun, it felt like being immersed in a brazier. And I was still wearing a thick camel hair robe. Yes, it had become my only companion. Otherwise, I had nothing of value. Every stranger passing by, whether going with or against the flow, stared at me with peculiar eyes. From these many gazes, I gleaned two different impressions. One probably thought I had typhoid fever and was afraid of the cold. The other clearly carried contempt and disdain. After seeing me, a poor wretch wearing a cotton-padded jacket in the summer heat, they would proudly glance back at their own silk or satin, thin, in-season attire. They felt immense glory, followed by a smug smile on their faces. Especially the noble ladies, barefoot, with their knees to their chests also exposed. Not to mention their shawls. So I faintly felt humiliating insults, and from the agitation of the insults, a kind of hatred and anger arose. But in a flash, I felt relieved again. You be smug, I'll do my thing. It's all nothing to do with me. Why get angry? The days of enjoyment won't last forever. Eventually, there will be a day when I step on the heads of these dogs and trample them severely!

I continued on my way, no longer thinking about those things, nor looking at those boring faces, pretending not to see them. While walking, I planned in my mind what words and methods to use to achieve the purpose of borrowing money. The weather was truly unbearably hot, and wearing that robe, like a quilt, almost made me faint. My undershirt was completely soaked with sweat, and every pore was desperately producing beads of sweat. The sweat on my forehead was like a torrential rain, constantly flowing down.

With great difficulty, I arrived at the house of the person I wanted to borrow money from. But as soon as I stepped through the door, I saw many boxes and luggage inside. Everyone was busy. I asked what was happening. It turned out the master was about to return to his hometown. Hearing this, my entire energy immediately cooled down. What to do? Could I even bring this up at this time? Seeing a continuous stream of people bringing gifts to see him off, I was the only exception. Thinking about it, there was no way I could say anything. It seemed hopeless. Moreover, I hadn't swallowed a grain of rice all day, and my vision was blurring in waves. In order to maintain appearances, knowing that I couldn't leave until I saw the master off to the ship, I waited and waited, sitting on pins and needles. During this time, I felt completely lost.

The master came out, saw me, and greeted me with a smile. I stood up emotionlessly and nodded. When he noticed me wearing that robe, he suddenly asked with concern: "It's so hot, and you're still wearing this. Are you not feeling well?"

"Um, um," I stuttered in reply. How could I explain?

The insults I encountered on the road were now being experienced again. Although the person asking might have been acting out of good intentions, I ultimately thought it was malicious.

When seeing the master off to the ship, on the ship, among a crowd of people, the master kept asking me if I was really not feeling well. How was I supposed to respond? Fine, I'll admit I'm not feeling well. But even so, I still couldn't cover up the embarrassing situation! The coldness and fickleness between people had been savored throughout this day, and this impression, similar to an insult, was more deeply engraved and not easy to forget than the one bestowed by strangers on the road.

Words Fail Me 277

— Firefly

Each day's bread must be dug out from under the pen. The ink in the inkwell has dried up, the nib is ruined, and my brain has been numbed by nicotine. This flesh and blood body is not a machine that can be driven by gasoline. I sit blankly at my writing desk, time slipping by like an arrow among the white clouds outside the window.

Words fail me.

Writing personal daily records has already been opposed. "Is there really not a single piece of important material in such a China, in such an era, for a supplement editor to collect and publish? Moreover, most of those articles record things that are mostly based on conjecture, and some are even the result of closed-door creation. Providing these false messages to readers seems inappropriate for an editor."

But you should write works of the times! Overthrow the capitalists! Workers of the world unite! Is that acceptable? Who isn't afraid of the bread-eating fellow moving the stage?

So the once-popular decadent, romantic works are the best strategy for writing articles. Beautiful little white doves! A woman's sexual desires! A bundle of love letters, and another bundle, can generate endless wealth. So many people talk about women, thinking it's a trouble-free way to take Jingzhou. But that fellow, a Gothic type who could distinguish the race of the opposite sex from a kiss, ran into a wall. Touching a woman's behind, like a native, is also not a business strategy.

The best material is naturally to grab someone's head and operate on it. The facts may be a hundred thousand miles away from the topic. From many big hats, draw soy sauce soup. After dozens of somersaults, the reader can't tell what it tastes like. But it's monopolized by the "special group." If you stand on their opposing front, you're either a "traitor" or a "spy." This kind of writing is writeable and unwriteable!

Some people also tell me it's best not to write. No matter how bad things get, don't move, don't move even a little! The method is certainly good. For example, after winning the lottery, throw the stick hiding the ticket into the Huangpu River. It's too far from the purpose of digging bread from under the pen. And cigarettes are very expensive. Why buy poison to kill the mosquitoes?

Words fail me. What should I do after all? The answer is an echo in the valley: What should I do after all?

Long-Distance Runner 278

— Qiu

Saints and Celebrities 279

— Juefu

It is people whose knowledge is deeper than ordinary people, whose learning is more profound than ordinary people, and whose virtue is nobler than ordinary people who are called saints. Once one becomes a saint, then every word and every sentence they utter must be regarded as the ultimate treasure, and every action and every movement is enough to be a model for thousands of generations. Confucius, the old master, is a saint, and is therefore respected as a teacher for all ages.

The so-called celebrities are different. Regardless of whether they are actually illiterate, regardless of their virtue and knowledge, regardless of how humble and shallow they are, and regardless of whether their rise to prominence is due to weapons, due to pens, due to business, ... as long as they can climb on top of a certain number of people, even the smallest details of their daily life are listed in the newspapers, they can be called celebrities.

The essence and growth of celebrities and saints are different, but the effect after their success is the same: because once a person becomes a celebrity, they seem to be omniscient and omnipotent. Every word they say is about benevolence and righteousness. As soon as they land in one place, everyone competes to treat them with reverence and spread their words everywhere. Moreover, everything they say and see is regarded as the ultimate truth and followed with sincerity. A financial tycoon can explain medical principles, a military leader can discuss educational rights and wrongs, a literary authority can talk about national defense plans, ... the reason is that they are celebrities.

Recently, no saints have appeared, and those who care about the world often can't help but lament their misfortune. However, with so many omniscient and omnipotent celebrities, what need is there for saints?

Rural Correspondence 280

— Want to Return

It has been three days since I arrived here, and I have been busy running around visiting the elders of my hometown, and I simply haven't had time to write to you. Today is the anniversary of my ancestor's death, and it has been seven years since I fulfilled my responsibility as a junior to kneel three times. My father told me the night before, so this afternoon I can sit peacefully at home for a day. At lunchtime, I went to the ancestral hall, and the old house looked even more dilapidated. It was slightly tilted, and the corners were occupied by spiders, showing the declining phenomenon of the village. The spirit tablets of the ancestors were in the center. I piously lit incense and candles and kowtowed. My father still stood woodenly on the side. He probably remembered the glory of building the ancestral hall? At that time, I was only two years old. Later, after I entered private school, he would have us sit next to his grand master's chair after every meal and lecture on the situation of the construction at the time. He would describe it from my perspective in detail, but I didn't understand as much as he said. It was like listening to a moving story. However, repeated lectures later became as annoying as listening to my family's long-term worker tell "Once upon a time, a family." But I still quietly watched my father's proud smile, for the sake of many dishes after drinking! Like edamame and peanuts, for me to chew slowly. My father, on the other hand, smoked his pipe and stroked the sparse beard under his chin. It can be seen that his lecture was not to let his seven- or eight-year-old son know how to build a great ancestral hall, but to narrate this amazing story to make himself feel extra happy, and to expand his son into a listening object.

Now, I see him standing motionless for a long time. I pity him [the original text is unclear here, with several characters obscured], wanting him to tell me about the situation at that time in detail.

In lonely sorrow, we left the ancestral hall and went home. My father drank alcohol at lunch. My father originally loved alcohol as much as his life. In recent years, my mother told me that he suddenly stopped drinking. When asked, he wouldn't give a reason. Today, he suddenly thought of drinking again. My mother seemed to want to ask, but finally didn't have the courage. My father had no expression, as if oppressed by deep sorrow. He finished a pot of alcohol in half the usual time. His face was flushed, his nerves were slightly excited, and he spoke calmly.

"You have been away for seven years. In these seven years, our town has changed greatly, and our family has fallen to this state. When you were young, I talked about the construction of the ancestral hall every day. You still have some images. Your grandfather was so impressive at that time. He established our surname X's family all by himself. He was also afraid of the decline of future generations, so he set up a charitable estate and built the ancestral hall on a larger scale. But now, the charitable estate has been stolen by unfilial descendants, and some have been sold. The ancestral hall is dilapidated, and none of the descendants can continue his efforts. They don't know [the original text is unclear here] Zhu's enterprise, gambling on tickets, so Sixth Elder Uncle, in order to reprimand Xingguan in the third room

Page 23

, became seriously ill and hasn't gotten out of bed yet... You, on the other hand, are respected by the clan. They say you are determined to study, and now you have graduated from university. I no longer have the money to cultivate you. I don't want you to be an official or anything. I just want you to revive my surname X's family, and it won't be in vain for my painstaking efforts..."

My father drank the remaining wine in his glass in one gulp and went back to his room to sleep in bed. My mother asked him if he wanted to eat, but he ignored her. He hoped so much that his son would be a great man who would revive the family, but this hope is probably forever a fantasy?

I can't bear to think about it, I can't bear to look at my father's wrinkled face without a trace of a smile!

Amateur Mailbox

Is This Also Environmental Oppression? 281

Editor:

I have a close friend who is very negative due to environmental oppression. His recent letters are so tragic that one can't bear to read them. If I don't find a way to help him, he may commit suicide. He is a man from an old-fashioned family, the eldest of two brothers. He is now twenty-three years old. At the age of nineteen, he was married by his parents' order and the words of a matchmaker. After the marriage, he went to the Japanese city to study. When he graduated from junior high school, his father was very unwilling for him to continue his studies, because his father had a store in the countryside, and no one was helping him. He managed everything by himself and wanted him to come back to help. But my friend is intelligent, has excellent literary skills, and is very ambitious. Not only was he unwilling to give up studying and become a merchant, but he also saw that the schools in City C were poorly managed, and he wanted to go to Beiping to continue his studies and strive for progress. Later, after asking a friend to request his father, he achieved his goal. Because the level of schools in the Japanese city was lower than that of schools in Beiping, he was demoted by one grade when he arrived in Beiping before being admitted to a famous high school. But in the second year of high school, he unfortunately failed two subjects and could not move up a class. The school has always been strict. If a student fails two subjects, they cannot move up a grade no matter what. Due to economic and age reasons, he could not afford to repeat a grade. However, the school was well-managed, and he was unwilling to leave the school. In this situation, he could not decide for himself and thought of returning home for the summer vacation to ask his father what to do. But he recalled the many difficulties and setbacks he had gone through to achieve his goal of coming here. Now that he cannot move up a grade, returning abruptly would mean that there would be no hope of coming back, and he would be criticized and have no face to see his father. Now he is in a dilemma and doesn't know what to do. He frowns all day long and is depressed. Knowing that you have great talent, I hope you will be happy to give me some guidance. I respectfully ask this, and wish you

Good health, Li Wenxiong

Answer: I think "your close friend" is really not worth it to be so decadent because he can't study at that school anymore. If you can't continue to study at that school, so be it. Is it necessary to be so troubled? Because the school is bad, you say that you can't study well in this kind of school, and you must change to another school. Because there is no opportunity to enter school, you say that you have no opportunity to study. These are all unpromising ideas and completely do not know what studying is all about. You must know that learning is something you have to pursue yourself. Having a school to enter certainly makes studying easier, but not having a school to enter does not mean there is no opportunity to study. As long as a person is willing to learn, they can create an environment for studying themselves. Edison is known to everyone. He did not enter any university, but he did succeed as a scientist. Of course, his research in science was more difficult and arduous than that of science university students, but because he was determined, he finally overcame those difficulties. Research in science requires experimental equipment. If I advise an ordinary person to study natural science on their own, they will definitely say, "I don't have the opportunity to go to school for experiments. Letting me study natural science on my own is just nice for you to say." But Edison at the beginning did not stop his ambition because of this difficulty. He just thought of a way to overcome it. If there was no experimental equipment, he would live a hard life and save money to buy some. So I think it is not necessary for your friend to be overly nostalgic and value the school. Not entering school cannot stop him from studying. I hope that he can seriously reflect on himself and see if there are any places where he has not worked hard and wasted energy in his past studies. If so, he must work harder and strive for improvement in the future. As for not being able to enter a certain famous high school again, or not being able to enter school, I think these are not a problem. We cannot treat ourselves as ducks, hoping to receive some "force-feeding" education. Studying is like a fish eating water in the water. You have to swim in the water and use your own mouth to absorb useful food.

Novel

Return (5) 282

— Written by Bulgarian Ivan Vazov, translated by Yang Sen

In the morning, Zuna went to the church very early. She took the franc given to her by Stoyan, bought candles, and lit one in front of every icon of St. He. When she came back, she seemed not as sad as before.

"Today is Christmas, so he will definitely come back... Holy Mary, send him back to me! My own dear angel... Lord Jesus, have mercy on me!"

Her daughter, Qina, reported that some people in the village had returned. The mother's face became even gloomier.

"Go welcome your brother, like the other girls," she said angrily to Qina.

"I want to go too, Mom," Radujo said, so the two children went to the snow-covered street, left the village market, and ventured onto the road. The mother stood at the door, waiting.

A blizzard blew down from the top of the mountain, and the valley and plain were all deeply covered with snow. A gloomy sky. A flock of crows flew over the road or perched on the tops of trees. On the road to Itihditing, there were black dots everywhere, representing the crowds waiting for the soldiers to arrive. These were all young girls, children, and old women. Because the soldiers were still coming constantly, some alone, some in groups of two or three. Qina and Radujo passed the first group of people, then the second group, and then the third group, standing far away on the road waiting. They wanted to be the first to see Stoyan. Although the falling snow almost blinded their eyes, they would immediately recognize him. The road stretched all the way to the small mountain and disappeared at that end. Qina and Radujo reached the top of the mountain, where the wind was even stronger, preventing them from moving forward. Two soldiers covered in snow walked past, but neither of them was Stoyan.

"Are there any more soldiers coming behind?" Qina asked.

"We don't know, children. Who are you waiting for?"

"Our brother." So the passersby walked past.

Qina still looked forward. She was cold and trembling, and Radujo was moaning, but her big brother was coming back. They had to greet him, otherwise their mother would be angry or cry.

Then they saw a carriage with two people inside, all dressed in warm clothes. Qina stood in front of the horse and stopped the carriage. "Sir, are there any soldiers behind you?"

"I don't know, my little dove," the man replied, half raising his leather hat and looking in surprise at the frozen little girl. So the carriage ran forward.
